text:
My husband & I really liked this simple pasta dish. I was hungry for something with pesto.  I made my own for this; my recipe produced about a cup of pesto and I ended up using it all; 1/2c didn't seem like enough.  I'm not used to using crushed red pepper flakes so wasn't certain how much to add; did about 1/4 tsp and it was just right; might do slightly more next time.  Sprinkled parmesan and toasted pine nuts on top of each serving.  YUMMO!  Thanks so much, Kristin! (My pesto recipe: 1/2c evoo, 1c fresh basil leaves, 1/2 tsp salt, 2 garlic cloves, 1/2c toasted pine nuts, 1/2c parmesan; blend all together in blender or food processor.)

text:
I have made this so many times!  People ALWAYS will ask you for the recipe!  The pesto sauce I use (classico brand) has tons of garlic, so I don't add any extra. Using bowties is a good idea, the sauce sticks good to this shape.  The sundried tomatoes in oil are the best, chopped small, with a little extra drizzle of the oil.  Adding fresh parmesan makes it happen!  Makes lots, cause it gets gobbled up!

text:
This is a good recipe.... I made a few modifications - I used 16 dry-packed sun-dried tomatoes instead of oil-packed (soaked them in boiling water for 3-5 minutes and then coarsely chopped) and added a handful of toasted pine nuts (omitted red pepper flakes though). Very easy and tasty.  I used half of a 270mL basil Classico pesto, if that helps anyone. :)

text:
I made this recipe last night, and both my husband and I really enjoyed it.  As others, I made a few changes - I used the oil from the sundried tomatoes, and I know I used more than 1 teaspoon, more like a couple of tablespoons - next time, I think I will saute in some chicken broth to cut the fat .  I also added some slice crimini mushrooms, some sliced roasted red peppers, more sundried tomatoes, and a sprinkle of parmesan. After the chicken and mushrooms were cooked, I tossed in the sundried tomatoes and red peppers, then tossed in the cooked whole wheat rotini pasta and the pesto, while keeping the pan on low. Tossing in a bowl would have been nicer presentation, but it was just the two of us, so I had one less bowl to wash.   I have never been a pesto fan, but I liked this.  It was not the best, as in 5 stars, but real close, It was relatively quick and easy to make and I will definitely make it again.

text:
I have been making this for several years and always use home made pesto. Sometimes I use dry packed sun dried tomatoes and soak them. I marinate the chicken (time permitting) in italian or balsamic dressing. If I have a zucchini I cube it and saute to add some veggies. Also if I have no fat sour cream will add a couple Tablespoons to the pot which makes it a bit creamy but doesn't change the great flavor. Since the pesto has parmesan I add feta to the finished dish. My grandson's favorite meal.

text:
I made this last night and it was good. I cook for my sister and myself and we both liked it (I must say that I surf the internet for recipes because she is very picky about what she'll eat and has a very limited palate, so I am constantly looking to add variety while cooking something she will like and eat).  I did alter the recipe some because it just didn't seem right. Number 1 was the amount of bow-tie pasta--I cut it in half. I flattened the chicken breasts and cooked them in the olive oil and garlic then removed from pan. Then added about 4oz. each of sliced mushrooms, grape tomatoes, and sliced red pepper to the pan and sauteed. Then I chopped the chicken into bite size pieces and combined all ingredients in a bowl with the pesto (from Costco, 1/2 cup plus 2 tbls). Garnished with fresh basil leaves, pine nuts, and parmasean cheese.  Added a side dish of steamed broccoli.  It was really delicious.  I really get my inspiration from the comments to the recipes on this site. With that in mind, I decided to write this, my first comment. Thank you to all of you fine cooks who take the time to write comments. I'm hooked.

text:
What isn't good with pesto? Right? I loved this. I am gluten and dairy free so I substituted the bow tie pasta with brown rice "spaghetti like" pasta 12oz. I was worried that 4oz less pasta would be an issue, but it was not. Not at all. I left out the sun-dried tomatoes (I just had them last night). I used an entire cup pesto, as opposed to 1/2c.  I also only used 1/4 tsp red pepper flakes. Next time, I will use more. Much more. I couldn't taste it. Maybe closer to a TBS. Not to over-do it because red pepper can steal a dish if over used.  The brown rice pasta actually gave this dish an extremely creamy texture. Which I absolutely loved. After boiling pasta, drain and rinse with cold water, but not too much. Just for 30 seconds or so tossing it with your hand. I added a dash of sea salt right before serving. Topped with toasted pine nuts. And YUM. I will make again.

text:
I tried this tonight as a friend of mine recommended it.  It was great, my husband loved it!  I also made a couple changes based on what I had on hand.  I had some sun dried tomato pesto as well as basil pesto(from Sprouts Natural market pre made).  I used the oil from both the basil and sun-dried tomato pesto to cook the chicken with the garlic, then added some sliced mushrooms and some sliced roasted red bell peppers. Once those were slightly wilted, I added the two different pestos (about 1/3 C basil and 1/3C Sun-dried pesto) I put the cooked pasta into the pan with all the other ingredients to absorb the liquids and added about 1/3 cup of grated parm/regianno.  Served it up with more Parm and it was awesome!  Be careful not to add too much cheese as it was a bit salty.

I make this all the time when short on available cooking time.  I usually make this with linquini, but any pasta would work really.  Also, although I prefer homemade pesto, the brand I found to be the closest to homemade is Del'Alpe brand.  Not a lot of 'extra' unnecessary stuff added to it.  Add some fresh broccoli to the pasta water when it is about 1/2 way through cooking and you've added a vegetable!  You can even leave out the sun dried tomatoes and red pepper flakes if you don't have it or like it.  A must to top with Parmesan or Romano when serving.

Substitute shrimp for the chicken and add the broccoli for an even tastier dish!

I already fed the kids something else that night, but after the youngest tried it, he told me to add it to his favorite meals to cook for him. This was so easy to prepare, the smells are delightful and between the appearance and taste, you would never know how easy it was to put together. The only change I will be making is not using a full package of sun-dried tomatoes, they were overpowering the flavor of the dish and we ended up eating around them.

Excellent!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!! I made a few changes to this recipe.   I only made this for 4 so I used 1/2 the box of bow tie. I used 3 garlic cloves. I used the oil from the sun-dried tomato jar to only cook the chicken a bit then added white wine. I put about 1/4 of a cup and then simmered the chicken for 10 minutes---wonderful flavor and very moist. I used double the amount of pesto and sun-dried tomatoes. I mixed it all and then added some of the white wine mixture from cooking the chicken just to add flavor and moisture. (I hate dry pasta). I also added a hefty amount of parm cheese, grated, didn't have the good stuff.   My family ate this in moments and wanted more. My husband is VERY picky and he loved it!!

I made this tonight.  Used 1/2 jar of sun dried tomatoes, drained, sauteed the chicken in the sundried oil with 1 tsp of garlic salt, ant pepper.  Cut into 1 inch bite size pieces with 4 cloves of garlic minced.  Sauteed for about 14 minutes, then added the sun dried tomatoes and pesto, a nice hand full of Romano cheese and about 2 tbs of evoo. Sauteed, cooked pasta, took one lade full of pasat water, added it and reduced to a nice thin sauce with a bit of a kick.  Major hit!!!

text:
Wonderful quick meal. I bought skinless chicken breast and wrapped them in plastic wrap and used my meat mallet to thin them out so they would cook faster and be juicy.. I hate dry chicken! Fortunately I saw my mother  using a meat mallet  growing up and everyone always wanted to know what her secret was to her meals being soooo juicy! After I cooked the chicken I added it to my pasta and then while the skillet was hot, I put the pesto sauce in the pan to warm it up along with a little can of peas and three diced sun dried tomatoes...after one minute I added this mixture to the pasta and chicken...I mixed it altogether then added 1/2 cup of mozzarella cheese and put  the lid on the pot so it would melt really well...this was amazing!!!!!! My husband really enjoyed it and my neighbor happen to come over to borrow something so I offered him a plate and he said it was great!!
Great recipe and if you enjoy sweet peas, add some, it really has a great taste w/the pesto!

I have to admit i used this more as inspiration, and made a few small adjustments. I did not have farfalle on hand, but had 1/2 pound of mini farfalle. I added diced onion, and additional sun dried tomato. Once the chicken, garlic and onion were cooked, I added the sun dried tomato and pesto to the saut pan with about 1/2 cup of the pasta water. Once that thickened, I added another 1/2 cup of pasta water, and a package of frozen peas. The pasta water created a nice sauce. Turned out very well.

text:
This is absolutely one of our family favorites, however I will never use prepared pesto sauce again having made it from scratch.  The pesto you buy in a jar at the grocery store tastes processed and there is a noticable difference when you use FRESH ingredients.  The fun thing about pesto is that you can use various types of nuts, cheeses and herbs provided you are willing to use the food processor. For basic pesto - I use fresh basil, Parmesan and Romano cheeses, garlic, fresh pepper, pine nuts and olive oil.  As you can see, it is simple to switch out any one of these ingredients (or add to it). For example, try walnuts instead of pinenuts or spinach instead of basil, other herbs, etc. Create your own master piece! I recently purchased my own basil plants because we use fresh basil in evertying from salads to sauces.  Enjoy!!!

text:
This recipe has a lot of good ideas, but the execution is a little lacking. For one, I halved the amount of pasta and I still thought the recipe was a little on the bland side. Adding some spices (salt,pepper,oregano) to the chicken before and/or while cooking makes a big difference. Also, the recipe calls for cooking the garlic and then cooking the chicken with the garlic still in the pan. In my opinion, that will lead directly to overcooked garlic. Cooking the chicken and then the garlic leads to a much tastier dish.

text:
Such a simple and delicious recipe!! I used oil from the tomatoes to cook the chicken, a generous seasoning of red pepper flakes (they add the perfect spice but its not overpowering at all) and a whole jar of Classico pesto (218ml) and we loved it! I do think the recipe is better is better with more pesto than called for, however it does state to adjust to your liking so it worked out perfectly with the jar size I bought-I used the called for amount of sun dried tomatoes because Im not a huge fan of them but theyre easy to eat around my husband loved them in this dish! You could use more or less to taste. We served with some fresh grated Parmesan cheese on top and loved it! I think the type of pesto you use will greatly influence the flavour of this dish, and Im sure its even better with fresh, but for a quick and easy weekday meal we enjoyed it with Classico basil pesto, and it didnt turn out oily like some other reviewers found. Will be a regular recipe in our house!

text:
This is a super delicious and easy dish. Like others, I made a few minor adjustments: I sauted  the boneless chicken breasts whole before cutting it up  which made them pjuicy. I added chopped yellow onion and garlic to the pan with the red pepper flakes for a couple minutes before I added the chicken to saut. I sprinkled the chicken with Italian seasoning, salt and pepper. After the chicken breasts were cooked through, I removed them to a plate and tented. Then I added asparagus (cut in 3 piieces), a few tablespoons of sun dried tomato bruschetta (so they were already chopped up) to the onion garlic mixture, sauted that all together and added a bit more red pepper flakes. When the asparagus was al dente, I removed the pan from the heat. I cut up the chicken and mixed everything (including accumulated juice from chicken) with the pasta and homemade pesto (used an easy NYT pesto recipe). Added fresh parm, salt and pepper and voila! A fine restaurant quality dinner. Will make again and again!

text:
This was a very good recipe just as it was presented. My rating is based upon that, although we did use a lot more pesto - because we had it on hand, fresh-made - and we added parmesan and mozzarella cheese and a few cherry tomatoes, halved, and added the mini-farfalle to the skillet so that it could all warm together.

When we make it again - and we will - I'm going to make some slight adjustments to fit our pallet and to avoid having to use more olive oil than is recommended (I did, and that made it a tad oily). Because we like sun-dried tomatoes, I'll probably use a half cup, finely chopped.  The big change I'll make is to steam the chicken breasts whole until almost done, let them cool, then cut them and add them to the pesto mix. This way, you don't have to cook the mixture very long or add oil to the pan beyond the recommendation.

Overall, a really good dish!

text:
Prepared as written, with store-bought pesto, too bland.  Pesto needs to either be increased by at least a third, or made fresh.  Some brands of farfalle (bow tie) pasta come in 12 oz. boxes, and perhaps that would be the right ratio of pasta to pesto.  Will try that next, as well as one more half chicken breast.  However, the olive oil then becomes too heavy so it is vital to remove all the oil from the sun dried tomato strips.  They also need to be chopped to add more flavor to each bite, rather than left julienned. Last, we needed to finish it with grated Parmesan cheese to give it more flavor.  Will make it again with the changes, since my family still liked (not loved) it.  Thank you!
